</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \lambda ^{d}-c_{1}\lambda ^{d-1}-c_{2}\lambda ^{d-2}-\cdots -c_{d}\lambda ^{0}=0.\,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle \lambda ^{d}-c_{1}\lambda ^{d-1}-c_{2}\lambda ^{d-2}-\cdots -c_{d}\lambda ^{0}=0.\,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c1e608521edb4daee039bdfe504a43306f61e653" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:39.791ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>The recurrence is <a href="/wiki/Stability_theory" title="Stability theory">stable</a>, meaning that the iterates converge asymptotically to a fixed value, if and only if the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eigenvalues" title="Eigenvalues">eigenvalues</a> (i.e., the roots of the characteristic equation), whether real or complex, are all less than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unity_(mathematics)" title="Unity (mathematics)">unity</a> in absolute value.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stability_of_linear_first-order_matrix_recurrences">Stability of linear first-order matrix recurrences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recurrence_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Stability of linear first-order matrix recurrences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Matrix_difference_equation" title="Matrix difference equation">Matrix difference equation</a></div>
<p>In the first-order matrix difference equation</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>∗<!-- ∗ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>A</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">[</mo>
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>∗<!-- ∗ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">]</mo>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle [x_{t}-x^{*}]=A[x_{t-1}-x^{*}]\,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="[x_{t}-x^{*}]=A[x_{t-1}-x^{*}]\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bc37b8a848f3a722b9e295fb37846aac022f9aac" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:24.846ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>with state vector <i>x</i> and transition matrix <i>A</i>, <i>x</i> converges asymptotically to the steady state vector <i>x</i>* if and only if all eigenvalues of the transition matrix <i>A</i> (whether real or complex) have an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_value" title="Absolute value">absolute value</a> which is less than 1.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stability_of_nonlinear_first-order_recurrences">Stability of nonlinear first-order recurrences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recurrence_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Stability of nonlinear first-order recurrences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Consider the nonlinear first-order recurrence</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x_{n}=f(x_{n-1}).}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x_{n}=f(x_{n-1})." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/91f76b42f234f94f0fc24136a163086d503bfc78" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:14.133ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>This recurrence is <a href="/wiki/Stability_theory" title="Stability theory">locally stable</a>, meaning that it <a href="/wiki/Limit_of_a_sequence" title="Limit of a sequence">converges</a> to a fixed point <i>x</i>* from points sufficiently close to <i>x</i>*, if the slope of <i>f</i> in the neighborhood of <i>x</i>* is smaller than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unity_(mathematics)" title="Unity (mathematics)">unity</a> in absolute value: that is,</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo>′</mo>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>∗<!-- ∗ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mo>&lt;</mo>
<mn>1.</mn>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |f'(x^{*})|&lt;1.\,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="|f'(x^{*})|&lt;1.\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fb07cb01dacbe5fd9b9f4d0e64b407eccac5e922" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.896ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>A nonlinear recurrence could have multiple fixed points, in which case some fixed points may be locally stable and others locally unstable; for continuous <i>f</i> two adjacent fixed points cannot both be locally stable.</p>
<p>A nonlinear recurrence relation could also have a cycle of period <i>k</i> for <i>k</i> &gt; 1. Such a cycle is stable, meaning that it attracts a set of initial conditions of positive measure, if the composite function</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>g</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>:=</mo>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo>∘<!-- ∘ --></mo>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo>∘<!-- ∘ --></mo>
<mo>⋯<!-- ⋯ --></mo>
<mo>∘<!-- ∘ --></mo>
<mi>f</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle g(x):=f\circ f\circ \cdots \circ f(x)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle g(x):=f\circ f\circ \cdots \circ f(x)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cb4b004d2740de93a11057409443fc768fbd4b5b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:24.45ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>with <i>f</i> appearing <i>k</i> times is locally stable according to the same criterion:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<msup>
<mi>g</mi>
<mo>′</mo>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>∗<!-- ∗ --></mo>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mo>&lt;</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |g'(x^{*})|&lt;1,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="|g'(x^{*})|&lt;1," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f3db7609bf813bcd6093e6284b867f5a720d714f" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.306ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>where <i>x</i>* is any point on the cycle.</p>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/Chaos_theory" title="Chaos theory">chaotic</a> recurrence relation, the variable <i>x</i> stays in a bounded region but never converges to a fixed point or an attracting cycle; any fixed points or cycles of the equation are unstable. See also <a href="/wiki/Logistic_map" title="Logistic map">logistic map</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dyadic_transformation" title="Dyadic transformation">dyadic transformation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tent_map" title="Tent map">tent map</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_to_differential_equations">Relationship to differential equations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recurrence_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Relationship to differential equations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When solving an <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_differential_equation" title="Ordinary differential equation">ordinary differential equation</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Numerical_ordinary_differential_equations" title="Numerical ordinary differential equations">numerically</a>, one typically encounters a recurrence relation. <p>Systems of linear first order differential equations can be discretized exactly analytically using the methods shown in the <a href="/wiki/Discretization" title="Discretization">discretization</a> article.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recurrence_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biology">Biology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recurrence_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Biology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some of the best-known difference equations have their origins in the attempt to model <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> dynamics. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Fibonacci_number" title="Fibonacci number">Fibonacci numbers</a> were once used as a model for the growth of a rabbit population.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Logistic_map" title="Logistic map">logistic map</a> is used either directly to model population growth, or as a starting point for more detailed models. In this context, coupled difference equations are often used to model the interaction of two or more populations. For example, the Nicholson-Bailey model for a host-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">parasite</a> interaction is given by</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>N</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>λ<!-- λ --></mi>
<msub>
<mi>N</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<msup>

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>a</mi>
<msub>
<mi>P</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
</mstyle>

</dl>
<p>with <i>N</i><sub><i>t</i></sub> representing the hosts, and <i>P</i><sub><i>t</i></sub> the parasites, at time <i>t</i>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Integrodifference_equation" title="Integrodifference equation">Integrodifference equations</a> are a form of recurrence relation important to spatial <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a>. These and other difference equations are particularly suited to modeling <a href="/wiki/Voltinism" title="Voltinism">univoltine</a> populations.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer_science">Computer science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recurrence_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Computer science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Recurrence relations are also of fundamental importance in <a href="/wiki/Analysis_of_algorithms" title="Analysis of algorithms">analysis of algorithms</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> If an <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithm</a> is designed so that it will break a problem into smaller subproblems (<a href="/wiki/Divide_and_conquer_algorithm" title="Divide and conquer algorithm">divide and conquer</a>), its running time is described by a recurrence relation.</p>
<p>A simple example is the time an algorithm takes to find an element in an ordered vector with <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.405ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> elements, in the worst case.</p>
<p>A naive algorithm will search from left to right, one element at a time. The worst possible scenario is when the required element is the last, so the number of comparisons is <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.405ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>.</p>
<p>A better algorithm is called <a href="/wiki/Binary_search_algorithm" title="Binary search algorithm">binary search</a>. However, it requires a sorted vector. It will first check if the element is at the middle of the vector. If not, then it will check if the middle element is greater or lesser than the sought element. At this point, half of the vector can be discarded, and the algorithm can be run again on the other half. The number of comparisons will be given by</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{1}=1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c_{1}=1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/11c8046c70c7e0e84425b052f781db3fc6dc4cb9" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.361ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span></dd>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>+</mo>
<msub>
<mi>c</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c_{n}=1+c_{n/2}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c_{n}=1+c_{n/2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/699eabecf7168ae8722419e7f516d7734ec2f7b6" style="vertical-align: -1.171ex; width:13.278ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>which will be close to <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>log</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \log _{2}(n)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\log _{2}(n)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f4e7727d9ed8daee1d80207aba949782dccf9547" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:7.3ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_signal_processing">Digital signal processing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recurrence_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Digital signal processing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Digital_signal_processing" title="Digital signal processing">digital signal processing</a>, recurrence relations can model feedback in a system, where outputs at one time become inputs for future time. They thus arise in <a href="/wiki/Infinite_impulse_response" title="Infinite impulse response">infinite impulse response</a> (IIR) <a href="/wiki/Digital_filter" title="Digital filter">digital filters</a>.</p>
<p>For example, the equation for a "feedforward" IIR <a href="/wiki/Comb_filter" title="Comb filter">comb filter</a> of delay <i>T</i> is:</p>
<dl>
<dd><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>y</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>α<!-- α --></mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>+</mo>
<mi>α<!-- α --></mi>
<msub>
<mi>y</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>T</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y_{t}=(1-\alpha )x_{t}+\alpha y_{t-T}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y_{t}=(1-\alpha )x_{t}+\alpha y_{t-T}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b59b6af119c2d1ebcc1ec11b924a47806c85c6ee" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:23.4ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd>
</dl>
<p>Where <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x_{t}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x_{t}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f279a30bc8eabc788f3fe81c9cfb674e72e858db" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.173ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the input at time <i>t</i>, <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y mw-math-element" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>y</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>t</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y_{t}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y_{t}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-math-element" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0fe9554452b93508c9d2479414a45981ecc75a2d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.983ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the output at time <i>t</i>, and α controls how much of the delayed signal is fed back into the output. From this we can see that</p>

<p>etc.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Recurrence_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Recurrence relations, especially linear recurrence relations, are used extensively in both theoretical and empirical economics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In particular, in macroeconomics one might develop a model of various broad sectors of the economy (the financial sector, the goods sector, the labor market, etc.) in which some agents' actions depend on lagged variables. The model would then be solved for current values of key variables (interest rate, real GDP, etc.) in terms of <a href="/wiki/Exogeny" title="Exogeny">exogenous variables</a> and lagged <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endogeneity_(economics)" title="Endogeneity (economics)">endogenous</a> variables. See also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_series_analysis" title="Time series analysis">time series analysis</a>.</p>

Simulation, Modelling and Optimization, SMO'06</i>. pp. 399–404.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARecurrence+relation&amp;rft.atitle=Using+generating+functions+to+solve+linear+inhomogeneous+recurrence+equations&amp;rft.aufirst=Tang&amp;rft.aulast=Minh&amp;rft.au=Van+To%2C+Tan&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.wseas.us%2Fe-library%2Fconferences%2F2006lisbon%2Fpapers%2F517-481.pdf&amp;rft.jtitle=Proc.+Int.+Conf.+Simulation%2C+Modelling+and+Optimization%2C+SMO%2706&amp;rft.pages=399-404&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
